+# JVM Squad — Team Personas
+
+> **Domain:** JVM backend services (Java 17+, Spring Boot, Quarkus) —
+> layered service architecture, JPA/Hibernate persistence, and the
+> testing discipline that keeps both honest.
+> **Squad contract:** ADR-009 (5 personas / 3 skills / ≥10 pitfalls /
+> ≥2 task chains / 1 example plan).
+> **VETO holders:** Language & Persistence Steward (schema migrations,
+> entity mappings, transaction boundaries), Service & API Architect
+> (public API contract changes, security-sensitive filters), Test &
+> Release Engineer (merging service code without slice/integration
+> coverage; weakening CI test gates).
+
+This squad layers JVM-specific archetypes onto the universal team in
+`.claude/team.md` (recommended foundational profile:
+`--profile core,jvm`).
+
+All personas are **fictional composites** per ADR-009 §positioning
+invariants — never use real people's names.
+
+---
+
+### 1. Beatriz Fontoura — Head of JVM Platform
+
+- **Reports to:** CEO
+- **VETO holder:** No (escalates VETO conflicts to CEO)
+- **Background:** 15 years running Java platforms — two banks, one
+  logistics unicorn. Led a 40-service Spring Boot estate through the
+  Java 8 → 17 migration and lived to write the runbook. Keeps a
+  spreadsheet of every dependency's EOL date.
+- **Focus:** Cross-cutting service reliability, JDK and framework
+  version strategy, dependency and CVE upgrade cadence, build health
+  (Maven/Gradle), choosing between Spring Boot and Quarkus per
+  workload, capacity planning.
+- **Anti-patterns she rejects:** framework upgrades without a
+  regression-test gate; "temporary" snapshot dependencies in a release
+  build; services pinned to an EOL JDK; adopting a new framework
+  feature before its first patch release without a rollback plan.
+- **Mantra:** "A JVM estate ages like a bridge — you either schedule
+  the maintenance or the maintenance schedules you."
+
+### 2. Tomasz Zieliński — Language & Persistence Steward (VETO)
+
+- **Reports to:** Head of JVM Platform
+- **VETO holder:** YES — any schema migration, entity-mapping change,
+  or transaction-boundary change on a production data path.
+- **Background:** 12 years of Java, the last 6 rescuing Hibernate
+  estates: un-EAGER-ing collections, rewriting `ORDINAL` enums before
+  someone reordered them, and converting `ddl-auto: update` shops to
+  Flyway. Reads generated SQL the way others read stack traces.
+- **Focus:** Java 17+ language conventions (records, sealed types,
+  pattern matching), JPA/Hibernate entity design, N+1 prevention,
+  transaction scope and propagation, migration discipline
+  (Flyway/Liquibase), HikariCP sizing. Primary owner of
+  `java-coding-standards`.
+- **VETO triggers (block if ANY):**
+  - `EnumType.ORDINAL` on any persisted enum, or a migration that
+    reorders an enum already persisted ordinally
+  - Hibernate `ddl-auto` set to anything but `none`/`validate` in a
+    production profile
+  - A destructive or non-reversible migration (column drop, type
+    narrowing) shipped in the same release as the code that stops
+    using it
+  - `EAGER` fetch on a collection association, or a new read path with
+    no fetch plan (JOIN FETCH / projection / EntityGraph) stated
+  - Remote I/O (HTTP, queue publish) inside a `@Transactional` scope
+- **Mantra:** "The database outlives every service that talks to it —
+  break the schema and you break the future."
+
+### 3. Priya Raghunathan — Service & API Architect (VETO)
+
+- **Reports to:** Head of JVM Platform
+- **VETO holder:** YES — any breaking change to a published API
+  contract, and any change to security-sensitive request-path
+  infrastructure (auth filters, rate limiting, forwarded-header
+  handling).
+- **Background:** Built public APIs at a payments provider where a
+  contract break meant partner outages and penalty clauses. Once
+  traced a fraud spike to a rate limiter keyed on a client-supplied
+  `X-Forwarded-For` — now audits every filter chain by hand.
+- **Focus:** Controller → service → repository layering, REST resource
+  shape and versioning, DTO/validation boundaries, centralised
+  exception handling (RFC 7807), caching and eviction strategy,
+  resilience (retries, circuit breakers), rate limiting. Primary
+  owner of `springboot-patterns`.
+- **VETO triggers (block if ANY):**
+  - Removing or renaming a field in a published response DTO without a
+    versioning or deprecation path
+  - A JPA entity returned directly from a controller (wire format
+    coupled to the schema)
+  - A rate limiter or audit log keyed on a raw `X-Forwarded-For` read
+    without the trusted-proxy conditions in `springboot-patterns`
+  - Business logic in a controller or `@Transactional` on a controller
+    method
+  - A new outbound call with no timeout, retry budget, or fallback
+    stated
+- **Mantra:** "Your API is a promise strangers build businesses on —
+  break it deliberately or not at all."
+
+### 4. Kofi Mensah-Addo — Test & Release Engineer (VETO)
+
+- **Reports to:** Head of JVM Platform
+- **VETO holder:** YES — merging service code without slice or
+  integration coverage, and any weakening of a CI test gate
+  (skipping Testcontainers, raising flake retry counts, lowering
+  coverage thresholds) without an ADR.
+- **Background:** Inherited a 45-minute `@SpringBootTest`-everything
+  suite with a 12% flake rate; rebuilt it into a sliced pyramid that
+  runs in 6 minutes. Treats every `Thread.sleep` in a test as a bug
+  report against the author.
+- **Focus:** Test pyramid for JVM services — plain JUnit 5 units,
+  Spring Boot test slices (`@WebMvcTest`, `@DataJpaTest`),
+  Testcontainers integration tests, Quarkus `@QuarkusTest` + Dev
+  Services, test-data builders, flake elimination, JaCoCo/CI gates.
+  Primary owner of `jvm-testing`.
+- **VETO triggers (block if ANY):**
+  - A new endpoint or repository method with no failing-path test
+    (only the happy path covered)
+  - `@SpringBootTest` used where a slice test covers the behavior
+    (full-context tests reserved for genuine integration)
+  - Data-layer tests running against H2 while production runs a
+    different engine (Testcontainers with the real engine required)
+  - `Thread.sleep` for synchronization in any test (use Awaitility or
+    latches)
+  - Disabling, quarantining, or retry-wrapping a flaky test without a
+    linked root-cause ticket
+- **Mantra:** "A green suite you can't trust is worse than a red one —
+  at least the red one is telling the truth."
+
+### 5. Marta Krüger — Production Reliability Engineer
+
+- **Reports to:** Head of JVM Platform
+- **VETO holder:** No (consults Language & Persistence Steward on pool
+  or transaction changes; consults Service & API Architect on
+  timeout/resilience changes)
+- **Background:** SRE who has spent a decade reading GC logs and heap
+  dumps at 3 a.m. Diagnosed a pool-exhaustion cascade caused by one
+  missing `readOnly = true`. Owns the squad's dashboards and the
+  pager.
+- **Focus:** Observability (Micrometer metrics, structured logs,
+  distributed tracing), GC and heap tuning, HikariCP pool sizing
+  against actual concurrency, graceful shutdown, startup-time and
+  memory-footprint tuning (including Quarkus native image trade-offs),
+  incident response and post-mortems.
+- **Anti-patterns she rejects:** unbounded in-memory caches ("it's
+  just a `ConcurrentHashMap`"); pool sizes copied from blog posts
+  instead of measured concurrency; missing timeouts on any outbound
+  call; logging PII into structured fields; deploys with no
+  health/readiness distinction.
+- **Mantra:** "The heap dump never lies, but you have to capture it
+  before the restart."
+
+---
+
+## How the squad escalates
+
+1. Persistence / API-contract / test-gate VETOes → blocked at PR stage
+   by the named holder. CEO mediates conflicts; Owner makes the final
+   call only if VETO holders disagree.
+2. New endpoints: Service & API Architect approves the contract →
+   Language & Persistence Steward approves the data path → Test &
+   Release Engineer verifies the coverage → Production Reliability
+   Engineer verifies observability and timeouts → Head of JVM Platform
+   signs the release.
+3. Incident response: Production Reliability Engineer runs the
+   playbook and captures evidence (heap dumps, GC logs, pool metrics);
+   Language & Persistence Steward analyses query/transaction behavior;
+   Test & Release Engineer converts the root cause into a regression
+   test before the post-mortem closes.
+
+## What the squad does NOT cover
+
+- Frontend work of any kind (use `.claude/frontend-team.md` archetypes)
+- Non-JVM backends — Go, Python, .NET (use their own squads)
+- Kubernetes/platform infrastructure beyond what the service itself
+  configures (use core DevOps archetypes)
+- Data warehousing / analytics pipelines (use core data engineer)
+
+The squad assumes a build tool (Maven or Gradle), a CI runner, and a
+relational database already exist. Its deliverables make the services
+on top of them correct, observable, and safely testable.
+
+---
+
+## SKILL MAP (jvm domain)
+

+| `jvm-testing` | Kofi Mensah-Addo — Test & Release Engineer | Tomasz Zieliński — Language & Persistence Steward |
+

+

+| JDK/framework upgrades, dependency/CVE cadence, build health | **Head of JVM Platform** | `java-coding-standards` | Head of JVM Platform |

+          # Retry contract (ADR-163 invariant — EXACTLY 2 attempts, never
+          # more, never unbounded): contention is bursty, so one retry
+          # relocates the measurement to a different scheduler window.
+          # Each attempt is wall-capped (coreutils timeout 420s ~= 5.5x
+          # the 77s local N=200 cost) so a pathologically contended
+          # attempt 1 is killed in time for attempt 2 to run and two
+          # attempts always fit the job budget. A genuine regression
+          # shifts the whole distribution and fails BOTH attempts ->
+          # explicit exit 1 (fail-closed; NOT continue-on-error, no
+          # third-party retry action). Attempt percentiles go to the step
+          # summary whenever the attempt leaves a parseable report — a
+          # cap-killed attempt that leaves none is NOTED explicitly — so
+          # a green-on-attempt-2 pattern (drift toward the ceiling)
+          # stays visible.
+          run_gate() {
+            timeout 420 python3 .claude/scripts/profile-opus-4-7.py \
+              --hook-latency \
+              --latency-iterations 200 \
+              --p95-ceiling-ms 120 \
+              --p99-ceiling-ms 160 > "/tmp/hook-latency-attempt-$1.json"
+          }
+          publish() {
+            # Advisory logging only — never gates (any failure tolerated).
+            # A cap-killed (124) attempt may leave no report: that case is
+            # NOTED explicitly in the summary, never silently skipped
+            # (pair-rail round-1 finding #3b).
+            python3 - "$1" <<'PYSUM' || true
+          import json, os, sys
+          att = sys.argv[1]
+          out = os.environ.get("GITHUB_STEP_SUMMARY")
+          def note(text):
+              if out:
+                  with open(out, "a") as f:
+                      f.write(text + "\n")
+          try:
+              with open(f"/tmp/hook-latency-attempt-{att}.json") as f:
+                  d = json.load(f)
+          except Exception:
+              note(f"hook-latency attempt {att}: NO parseable report (a 420s cap-killed attempt leaves none)")
+              sys.exit(0)
+          rows = [f"| attempt {att}: {name} | {h.get('p50_ms')} | {h.get('p95_ms')} | {h.get('p99_ms')} | {h.get('max_ms')} |"
+                  for name, h in d.get("hooks", {}).items() if isinstance(h, dict) and "p95_ms" in h]
+          if rows:
+              note("| hook-latency entry | p50 | p95 | p99 | max (ms) |")
+              note("|---|---|---|---|---|")
+              note("\n".join(rows))
+          else:
+              note(f"hook-latency attempt {att}: report parsed but carries no per-hook stats (early-error report: {str(d.get('error','?'))[:120]})")
+          PYSUM
+          }
+          if run_gate 1; then
+            publish 1
+            echo "✓ hook latency p95/p99 within budget (attempt 1)"
+          else
+            rc=$?
+            publish 1
+            echo "::warning::hook-latency gate attempt 1 FAILED (exit $rc; 124 = 420s per-attempt cap) — single deterministic retry (PLAN-159/ADR-163; a real regression fails both attempts)"
+            if run_gate 2; then
+              publish 2
+              echo "✓ hook latency p95/p99 within budget (attempt 2 — attempt 1 was a load-flake; see ::warning)"
+            else
+              rc2=$?
+              publish 2
+              echo "::error::hook-latency gate FAILED on BOTH attempts (rc1=$rc rc2=$rc2) — treating as a real regression"
+              exit 1
+            fi
+          fi
 
       - name: Run profile-opus-4-7.py --floor (sanity)
         run: |

     2	# =============================================================================
     3	# wave1-wrapper-matrix-proof.sh — PLAN-159 Wave 1: retry-wrapper truth table.
     4	#
     5	# Repeatable proof (pair-rail round-1 finding #3a: "proven by test" must be
     6	# a runnable artifact, not a session anecdote). Applies the STAGED patch to
     7	# a temp copy of validate.yml, extracts the REAL step run-block, replaces
     8	# run_gate with a mock, and asserts the full truth table:
     9	#
    10	#   pass@1                 -> exit 0
    11	#   fail@1 + pass@2        -> exit 0  + ::warning logged
    12	#   fail@1 + fail@2        -> exit 1  + ::error logged     (fail-closed)
    13	#   fail@1 no-report + ... -> publish() notes "NO parseable report"
    14	#
    15	# Run by land-plan159.sh as a pre-commit gate; also runnable standalone.
    16	# READ-ONLY on the repo: everything happens in a mktemp dir.

    19	
    20	REPO="$(cd "$(dirname "${BASH_SOURCE[0]}")/../../.." && pwd)"
    21	STAGED="$REPO/.claude/plans/PLAN-159/staged/wave1"
    22	TMP="$(mktemp -d)"
    23	trap 'rm -f "$TMP"/* 2>/dev/null; rmdir "$TMP" 2>/dev/null || true' EXIT
    24	say() { printf '\033[1;36m==> %s\033[0m\n' "$*"; }
    25	die() { printf '\033[1;31mFATAL: %s\033[0m\n' "$*" >&2; exit 1; }

    30	# could already be patched, and re-applying would fail spuriously. HEAD
    31	# is patch-clean by construction until the ceremony commit lands, which
    32	# also means: this proof is a PRE-LAND gate only (post-land, HEAD already
    33	# carries the new step and the patch no longer applies).
    34	git -C "$REPO" show HEAD:.github/workflows/validate.yml > "$TMP/validate.yml"

    42	shutil.move("validate.yml", ".github/workflows/validate.yml")

   350	        "hook_event_name": "PostToolUse",
   351	        "tool_name": "Bash",

   357	
   358	def run_hook_latency(
   359	    repo_root: Path,
   360	    iterations: int = 200,
   361	    p95_ceiling_ms: float = 120.0,
   362	    p99_ceiling_ms: float = 160.0,
   363	) -> Dict[str, Any]:
   364	    """Subprocess-profile the hook-latency corpus and gate p95/p99.
   365	
   366	    Addresses E12-F4 (profile-opus-4-7.py had zero latency thresholds) and
   367	    PLAN-154 binding constraint 8 / SENT-F MANIFEST open-issue 3 (the observe
   368	    rail's extended write path must join this corpus).
   369	
   370	    Corpus (each entry: N+1 runs, first discarded as cold, warm p95/p99
   371	    asserted against the shared ceilings):
   372	
   373	    1. ``check_agent_spawn``                      — original E12-F4 entry.
   374	    2. ``check_anti_ceo_overhead[observe=unset]`` — PreToolUse record_pre
   375	       carrier, observe rail structurally OFF (baseline).
   376	    3. ``check_anti_ceo_overhead[observe=1]``     — same, CEO_LEARNING_OBSERVE=1.
   377	       record_pre is contractually byte-identical (MF-SEC-5), so this state
   378	       must sit at baseline; the run doubles as an MF-SEC-5 tripwire (no
   379	       observation store may appear on the Pre side).
   380	    4. ``check_output_secrets[observe=unset]``    — PostToolUse record_post
   381	       host, observe OFF. Negative control: the per-entry isolated audit dir
   382	       must contain NO ``*.observe.jsonl`` after the runs (A12 zero-delta).
   383	    5. ``check_output_secrets[observe=1]``        — THE extended write path.
   384	       Each timed run is pre-seeded (unmeasured check_anti_ceo_overhead run,
   385	       same tool_use_id) so record_post takes the real paired path: pairing
   386	       pop + eviction save + lifecycle emit + observe append. Positive
   387	       control (anti-vacuity, S254 class): when the repo's tool_lifecycle.py
   388	       ships the observe rail, the store MUST hold >= iterations rows, all
   389	       ``"paired": true`` — otherwise the entry measured a no-op boolean and
   390	       the gate FAILS rather than passing vacuously. On a tree without the
   391	       rail (pre-PLAN-154 landing) the control is reported not-required and
   392	       both states measure baseline parity.
   393	
   394	    Isolation: every corpus entry gets its own throwaway HOME +
   395	    CEO_AUDIT_LOG_DIR (never the real ``~/.claude``); CEO_SOTA_DISABLE /
   396	    CEO_TOOL_LIFECYCLE / CEO_ANTI_OVERHEAD / CLAUDE_SESSION_ID are scrubbed
   397	    from the inherited env so the measured state is deterministic.
   398	
   399	    Budget: p95 < 120ms / p99 < 160ms per corpus entry — the CI-confirmed
   400	    fallback budget from PLAN-063 DIM-15 (ubuntu-latest baseline 57-64ms +
   401	    headroom). More conservative than the test_hook_latency.py xfail budget
   402	    (p95 100ms / p99 150ms) to absorb profile-script measurement variance.
   403	
   404	    Returns a dict with per-hook p50/p95/p99 (``hooks``), the two observe
   405	    controls (``controls``), the legacy top-level ``check_agent_spawn``
   406	    block (back-compat), and an aggregate ``passed`` boolean.
   407	    """
   408	    hooks_dir = repo_root / ".claude" / "hooks"
   409	    agent_spawn = hooks_dir / "check_agent_spawn.py"
   410	    anti_overhead = hooks_dir / "check_anti_ceo_overhead.py"
   411	    output_secrets = hooks_dir / "check_output_secrets.py"
   412	    measured_at = datetime.now(timezone.utc).strftime("%Y-%m-%dT%H:%M:%SZ")
   413	
   414	    # ADR-163 percentile precondition (PLAN-159 debate round-1 must-fix):
   415	    # with the nearest-rank truncation in _pct_of_sorted (int((n-1)*p/100)),
   416	    # p95 and p99 collapse onto the SAME order statistic for n < 22 — the
   417	    # p99 ceiling becomes dead code and the gate keys on the 2nd-largest
   418	    # sample (the S272/S273 load-flake class). A gate run on a collapsed
   419	    # index is a defect state: fail LOUDLY instead of measuring.
   420	    idx_p95 = int((iterations - 1) * 95 / 100.0)
   421	    idx_p99 = int((iterations - 1) * 99 / 100.0)
   422	    if idx_p95 == idx_p99:
   423	        return {
   424	            "schema": "profile-opus-4-7.v1",
   425	            "mode": "hook_latency",
   426	            "measured_at": measured_at,
   427	            "error": (
   428	                "percentile_indices_collapsed: iterations=%d puts p95 and "
   429	                "p99 on the same order statistic (index %d); minimum is 22, "
   430	                "gate standard is 200 (ADR-163)" % (iterations, idx_p95)
   431	            ),
   432	            "p95_ceiling_ms": p95_ceiling_ms,
   433	            "p99_ceiling_ms": p99_ceiling_ms,
   434	            "passed": False,
   435	        }
   436	
   437	    for required in (agent_spawn, anti_overhead, output_secrets):
   438	        if not required.is_file():
   439	            return {
   440	                "schema": "profile-opus-4-7.v1",
   515	            "hook": output_secrets,
   516	            "payload": _latency_post_payload,
   517	            "env_set": {"CEO_LEARNING_OBSERVE": "1"},
   518	            "seed": True,
   519	        },
   520	    ]
   521	
   522	    observe_store_name = _LATENCY_SESSION_ID + ".observe.jsonl"
   523	    hooks_out: Dict[str, Dict[str, Any]] = {}
   524	    all_within_budget = True
   525	
   526	    for entry in corpus:
   527	        entry_tmp = Path(tempfile.mkdtemp(prefix="ceo-hook-latency-"))
   528	        try:
   529	            env = dict(base_env)
   530	            env["HOME"] = str(entry_tmp / "home")
   531	            env["CEO_AUDIT_LOG_DIR"] = str(entry_tmp / "audit")
   532	            env.update(entry["env_set"])
   533	            (entry_tmp / "home").mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)
   534	            (entry_tmp / "audit").mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)
   535	
   536	            # Codex pair-rail S265 P2: a hook that exits non-zero (import
   537	            # or runtime error) must FAIL the gate, not silently record a
   538	            # small latency sample. Hooks always exit 0 by contract, so any
   539	            # non-zero return is a real failure — capture it for seed AND
   540	            # timed runs and fold it into entry_passed (the S254 vacuous-
   541	            # green class this profiler exists to prevent).
   542	            entry_hook_failed = False
   543	
   544	            def _run_once(tag: str) -> float:
   545	                nonlocal entry_hook_failed
   546	                tool_use_id = "profile-tu-" + tag
   547	                if entry["seed"]:
   548	                    # Unmeasured Pre stamp via the REAL record_pre carrier so
   549	                    # the timed record_post run takes the paired path.
   550	                    # ADR-163: a >10s stall is folded into the fail-closed
   551	                    # sink instead of raising an opaque TimeoutExpired
   552	                    # traceback (more subprocess calls at N=200 raise the
   553	                    # cumulative odds of one stall on a contended runner).
   554	                    try:
   555	                        seed_res = subprocess.run(
   556	                            [sys.executable, str(anti_overhead)],
   557	                            input=_latency_pre_payload(tool_use_id),
   558	                            capture_output=True,
   559	                            env=env,
   560	                            cwd=str(repo_root),
   561	                            timeout=10,
   562	                        )

   829	                    result.get("hooks", {}).items()
   830	                ):
   831	                    if not stats.get("passed", True):
   832	                        failures.append(
   833	                            f"{hook_name} p95={stats['p95_ms']:.1f}ms "
   834	                            f"p99={stats['p99_ms']:.1f}ms"
   835	                        )
   836	                for ctrl_name, ctrl in sorted(
   837	                    result.get("controls", {}).items()
   838	                ):
   839	                    if isinstance(ctrl, dict) and not ctrl.get("passed", True):
   840	                        failures.append(f"control:{ctrl_name}")
   841	                print(
   842	                    "FAIL: hook latency gate — "
   843	                    + ("; ".join(failures) or result.get("error", "unknown"))
   844	                    + f" (ceilings p95<{result.get('p95_ceiling_ms')}ms / "
   845	                    f"p99<{result.get('p99_ceiling_ms')}ms)",
   846	                    file=sys.stderr,
   847	                )
   848	                return 1
   849	            return 0
   850	    except Exception as exc:  # noqa: BLE001 — top-level safety net
